Please note that some courses might overlap between the two majors, so make sure they do not count towards both requirements. If you have any questions regarding the specific requirements or course equivalencies, please consult with your academic advisor. Good luck with your graduation!

### Question 2: Can you differentiate a cross-listed course and elective applied course in the case of a double major?  
### Answer: 

Yes, you can differentiate a cross-listed course and an elective applied course in the case of a double major.

Cross-listed courses:
- These are courses that are shared between two majors or a major and a minor.
- Up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements for each pair of majors (or major and minor).
- This limit applies per each pair of majors (or major and minor).

Elective applied courses:
- These are courses from other majors that emphasize the applications of Mathematics.
- Students must take at least 2 applied courses (at least one at the 200 level).
- Prerequisites must be completed or instructor's approval is needed.
- Students cannot double count a course for two different requirements. For example, Operations research can only count for either 1 Advanced course or 1 Elective course, but not both. 

In summary, cross-listed courses are shared between majors/minors and can be double-counted within specific limits, while elective applied courses are focused on the application of mathematics and have specific requirements regarding prerequisites and double counting.  

<details>

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
and a minor) share cross- listed or tagged1 courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. This limit is per each pair of majors (or major and minor) and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. For example, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. This rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or tagged. For instance, if major A requires certain courses from major B for out-of-area foundation, exploration, or applications of the major, and these courses are not cross-listed between A and B, they do not count toward the 8-credit limit. 1 In interdisciplinary minors, the requirements mainly consist of courses from other majors. These courses are usually not cross-listed with the minors and are referred to as 'tagged' by these minors. 13.4  Experiential Learning Requirements Experiential Learning can

### Question 3: I would like to ask for the capstone withdrawal policy. What will be the impact when I choose to drop the capstone before the Fall 2025 term starts? Will there be any penalties associated with withdrawing, such as a 'W' notation on my transcript?  
### Answer: 

Based on the provided context, the capstone withdrawal policy does not specifically mention the withdrawal process for the Capstone course before the Fall 2025 term starts. However, generally speaking, for regular courses, the policy states that a "W" grade will be recorded on the transcript for withdrawals between Week 5 and Week 8 of the term, which does not affect the student's GPA.

If you withdraw from the Capstone course before the Fall 2025 term starts, it likely falls outside the defined withdrawal periods mentioned in the document. Therefore, it is possible that you might receive a different grade or penalty, but this is not explicitly stated in the given context.

To get accurate information regarding the specific withdrawal policy for the Capstone course before the Fall 2025 term starts, you should consult with your Academic/Major Advisor or refer to the official university policies or guidelines. They can provide you with the most precise and up-to-date information. Additionally, they can help you understand any potential impacts on your academic records and enrollment status. 

In summary, there is no direct mention of penalties or 'W' notation for withdrawing before the Fall 2025 term starts, but it is advisable to seek clarification from your advisor or the registrar's office.

### Question 4: Questions related to course history, in which one course can have multiple IDs? Like Advanced Deep Learning course. How would it be handled among different cohorts?  
### Answer: 

When a course like Advanced Deep Learning has multiple IDs and is offered to different cohorts, it is typically handled by maintaining separate records for each cohort. Each cohort would have its own unique identifier within the system, ensuring that all activities, grades, and progress of students in that specific cohort are tracked accurately. This approach allows for the management of course history effectively, even when multiple IDs are used for the same course content across different groups of students. Thus, questions related to course history can be answered accurately by referencing the specific cohort ID associated with the student's participation in the course.

### Question 5: I have taken Microeconomic Analysis and Macroeconomic Analysis in Fall 2023. Am I eligible to take Financial Economics in Spring 2024?  
### Answer: 

Yes, you are eligible to take Financial Economics in Spring 2024. According to the provided information, advanced courses in Economics, such as Financial Economics, can be taken after completing at least one of Microeconomic and Macroeconomic Analysis and Econometrics. Since you have already completed Microeconomic Analysis and Macroeconomic Analysis, you meet the prerequisite requirements for taking Financial Economics. However, note that Econometrics is also listed as a prerequisite, so you would need to ensure that you have completed Econometrics or another equivalent course to fully meet the eligibility criteria. Assuming you have completed Econometrics, you should be able to enroll in Financial Economics. If not, you may need to wait until you have completed the required prerequisites.

This course focuses on the macroeconomic tools of government – fiscal and monetary policy – and their effects on long-run economic growth, employment, and inflation.

### Question 6: If I have waived the course Computer Science I, but I want to declare Computer Science major, do I have to take Computer Science I?  
### Answer: 

Yes, you have to take Computer Science I if you want to declare Computer Science as your major. Waiving the course does not exempt you from this requirement. The context states that all students are encouraged to take the course Introduction to Computer Science first to explore all different areas of computer science, and it is a foundational course required for the major. Therefore, even if you have waived the course, you still need to complete it to meet the major requirements.

### Question 7: If I have taken the following courses: Mathematical Statistics, Abstract Algebra, Linear Algebra, Multivariable Calculus, Calculus, Differential Equation, Stochastic Calculus, Statistical Learning, Discrete Mathematics, Probability, am I eligible to declare a minor in Applied Mathematics? What about majoring in Applied Mathematics?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided, you have taken several foundational and intermediate courses in mathematics, which are essential for declaring a minor in Applied Mathematics. Here's a breakdown of your eligibility:

### Minor in Applied Mathematics:
- **Eligibility**: Yes, you are eligible to declare a minor in Applied Mathematics.
  - You have already taken several core courses like **Mathematical Statistics**, **Linear Algebra**, **Multivariable Calculus**, **Calculus**, **Differential Equation**, **Probability**, and **Discrete Mathematics**. These courses form a strong foundation for the minor.
  - You have also taken **Stochastic Calculus** and **Statistical Learning**, which are relevant to the applied aspects of mathematics.

However, to officially declare a minor, you still need to meet the specific requirements set by your institution. Typically, a minor requires completing a certain number of courses, including both foundational and intermediate courses. Since you have already taken many of these, you should consult with an academic advisor to confirm the exact requirements and ensure you meet them.

### Majoring in Applied Mathematics:
- **Eligibility**: It depends on the specific requirements of your institution.
  - To major in Applied Mathematics, you generally need to take additional advanced courses beyond what is required for the minor. Specifically, you need to take at least 2 advanced courses (300-level) and 2 applied courses (200-level or above).
  - You have already taken some advanced courses like **Stochastic Calculus** and **Statistical Learning**, but you might need to take more advanced courses such as **Advanced Statistics**, **Numerical Analysis**, **Optimization**, or **Partial Differential Equations**.
  - Additionally, you need to take at least 2 applied courses, such as those from economics, engineering, or computer science, which emphasize the application of mathematics.

Again, you should consult with an academic advisor to confirm the exact requirements for the major and ensure you meet them. 

In summary, you are eligible to declare a minor in Applied Mathematics, but you may need to take additional courses to major in it. Always consult with an academic advisor for precise guidance.

The primary objective of the History Major Capstone is for students to produce a body of original historical research based on primary source evidence. The project generally takes the form of an undergraduate thesis; however students may design a non-traditional project with a substantial written component (e.g., a documentary, a museum exhibit, a digital database, an oral history archive, etc.). Students will design their Capstone project in close consultation with history faculty and receive scaffolded peer-review in the research design seminar. Capstone projects should reflect student specialization in at least one geographical, temporal, or thematic historical field and are encouraged to apply historical perspectives to problems in other disciplines. ### Question 11: I have a question if I take a gap year, will my financial aid be canceled? If yes, can I still re-apply for the financial aid program when I get back to school?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided, taking a gap year does not directly lead to cancellation of financial aid. However, re-admission to full-time status requires reapplying for admission and financial aid. Therefore, you would need to go through the process of reapplying for financial aid when you return to school. Your academic record will remain unchanged upon reinstatement except under special circumstances decided by the Dean’s Office. It's important to meet with the Student Financial Services team early if you anticipate any issues with clearing your account balance on time. This proactive approach can help ensure a smooth re-entry into the program.

### Question 13: If I major in Economics, is it sufficient that I take Scholar Development to fulfill Experiential Learning requirements?  
### Answer: 

No, taking Scholar Development alone is not sufficient to fulfill the Experiential Learning requirements for an Economics major. According to the provided information, all full-time, undergraduate, degree-seeking students must complete at least 4 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the Experiential Learning Program (ELP) as a graduation requirement. The ELP streams are housed within Academic Affairs (AA), Career Services (CS), and Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation (CEI), and each team is responsible for administrative and academic duties of their respective stream(s). Therefore, completing Scholar Development would need to be part of one of these ELP streams to count towards the Experiential Learning requirements. Without this context, taking Scholar Development does not automatically fulfill the Experiential Learning requirements for an Economics major.  

<details>

### Question 14: Is it sufficient for me to complete 4 credits in EL if I major in Engineering?  
### Answer: 

Yes, it is sufficient for you to complete 4 credits in EL if you major in Engineering. According to the provided information, all full-time, undergraduate, degree-seeking students must complete at least 4 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the Experiential Learning Program (ELP) as a graduation requirement. Since you are majoring in Engineering, completing 4 credits in EL will meet this requirement. However, ensure that these credits are approved by the Chair of Engineering and count towards either elective or major requirements.

### Question 15: Can I take all four engineering foundation courses and only two intermediate engineering courses?  
### Answer: 

No, you cannot take all four engineering foundation courses and only two intermediate engineering courses. According to the provided information, you need to take at least three courses at the 300-level or Advanced level (which includes intermediate engineering courses) to fulfill the degree requirements. Therefore, taking only two intermediate engineering courses would not meet this requirement. You would need to take at least one more advanced course to satisfy the criteria.

### Question 16: If I have completed the course Intro to AI, will CS207 - Object-Oriented Analysis and Design and CS211 – Operating Systems suffice to fill the rest two intermediate courses?  
### Answer: 

Based on the provided information, completing CS204 (Introduction to Artificial Intelligence), CS207 (Software Construction), and CS211 (Operating Systems) does not necessarily mean you have fulfilled all the intermediate courses required for your program. 

CS207 and CS211 are listed as intermediate courses, but CS204 is already completed as per the question. However, there is no mention of what the other two intermediate courses are. Therefore, without knowing the specific names of the remaining two intermediate courses, it's impossible to definitively say whether CS207 and CS211 alone would suffice.

If the two remaining intermediate courses are different from CS207 and CS211, then they would need to be completed separately. If CS207 and CS211 are part of a set of three intermediate courses, then the third course would still need to be completed. 

In summary, based on the information given, CS207 and CS211 alone may or may not suffice depending on the specific requirements of the program. You would need to check the full list of intermediate courses required for your program to determine if these two courses are sufficient. The reference to CS208 (Machine Learning for Data) is irrelevant to answering this question.

(AI) is a research ﬁeld that studies how to realize the intelligent human behaviors on a computer. The ultimate goal of AI is to make a computer that can learn, plan, and solve problems autonomously. In this course, student will learn the foundational principles and practice implementing some of these applications including representation, problem solving, and learning methods of artiﬁcial intelligence. Accordingly, students should be able to develop intelligent systems by assembling solutions to concrete computational problems; understand the role of knowledge representation, problem solving, and learning in intelligent-system engineering; and appreciate the role of problem solving, vision, and language in understanding human intelligence from a computational perspective. ### Question 17: Does completing both Microeconomics and Macroeconomics satisfy the core theory requirement, or is an additional course needed?  
### Answer: 

Completing both Microeconomics and Macroeconomics satisfies the core theory requirement for the economics major. An additional course is not needed as long as these two courses are completed.

### Question 18: If I want to major in Engineering, can I choose other programming courses besides Computer Science I and Computer Science II, for instance Introduction to data visualization?  
### Answer: 

Yes, if you're majoring in Engineering, you can choose other programming courses besides Computer Science I and Computer Science II. For example, you can opt for Introduction to Data Visualization, which is listed as CS103: Programming for Data Science and Visualization. However, it's important to note that these courses may fulfill elective requirements rather than major course requirements. Always check your specific major's curriculum for detailed information. Other courses like CS101: Introduction to Programming and CS104: Introduction to Computer Science I can also be part of your electives or prerequisites for certain courses. Make sure to consult with an academic advisor to ensure your course selection aligns with your major's requirements. The provided context does not explicitly restrict Engineering majors from taking these courses, so they are generally open options for you.

### Question 19: Given I took Discrete Mathematics in Spring 2022 and earned B, then the same course in Spring 2024 and earned C-, which grades will be kept?  
### Answer: 

The higher grade, which is the B from Spring 2022, will be kept and used in the GPA calculation. The lower grade, which is the C- from Spring 2024, will be overwritten by the notation "RP", meaning "repeated", and remain on the transcript.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
advisor, the course instructor, and the Registrar’s Office. Considerations will include course availability and capacity in the next academic term or next academic year. A higher grade will be kept and used in the GPA calculation. The lower grade will be overwritten by the notation “RP”, meaning “repeated”, and remain on the transcript. Credits of the repeated course are counted toward the total attempted credits. ### Question 20: Can I register 300-level math courses as exploratory courses E4?  
### Answer: 

No, you cannot register 300-level math courses as exploratory courses E4. The context specifies that exploratory courses for E4-Mathematics and Computing are limited to 100-level or 200-level courses. Therefore, 300-level courses do not qualify for this category.

### Question 21: Can I register for more than 20 credits in a semester?  
### Answer: 

No, you cannot register for more than 20 credits in a semester according to the given context. The maximum course load per term is 20 credit hours, and students wishing to register for more than this amount must submit the Petition for Alternative Course Load or Maximum Course Load Request form to the Registrar's Office, which requires approval from the Academic/Major Advisor.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 7]

In order to make standard progress toward completing the degree, students are required to register for no fewer than 12 credit hours and no more than 20 credit hours per term. Students who wish to take fewer than 12 or more than 16 credit hours in one term must submit the Petition for Alternative Course Load or Maximum Course Load Request form to the Registrar's Office. The request form must be approved and signed by the Academic/Major Advisor before submission. Students on a Leave of Absence (see Section 9) are considered to be still enrolled in the Fulbright undergraduate program during the period of the leave, though they are not registered for any courses. ### Question 22: What is the maximum number of times I can retake a course to improve my grade, and how does it affect my transcript?  
### Answer: 

You can retake a course up to three times. If you retake the same course for the third time, it must be due to failing the second time or needing a specific grade to meet major requirements. A higher grade will be kept and used in the GPA calculation, while the lower grade will be overwritten by the notation "RP", meaning "repeated", and remain on the transcript. Credits of the repeated course are counted toward the total attempted credits. For courses not in your major or minor, you might be able to request a third retake under special circumstances after consulting with your academic/major advisor, the course instructor, and the Registrar's Office.

### Question 23: For a student doing the literature capstone, if a student includes charts or tables, do they count toward the word limit?  
### Answer: 

Charts or tables do not count toward the word limit for a student doing the literature capstone, according to the guidelines provided. Specifically, the word count regulations state that submissions should be 10,000-15,000 words, including endnotes or footnotes, but not including full bibliography and images with captions. Therefore, charts or tables would be considered images with captions and thus do not contribute to the word count.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: VIETNAM STUDIES CAPSTONE GUIDELINES.pdf, Page: 10]
2. Capstone by Thesis Guidelines: 2.1. Word Count Regulations The ﬁnal submission should be 10,000-15,000 words, including endnotes or footnotes, but not including full bibliography and images with captions. The bibliography must include a minimum of 25 primary and secondary sources that are referenced in the development of the thesis or capstone project. Submissions that fall short of or exceed the allowed word count range will not be accepted. If the length requirements are not met, a justiﬁcation should be provided. 2.2. 2. Capstones by Thesis guidelines: 2.1. Word count regulations The written thesis is documentation of the capstone project, in the form of a research paper. ### Question 24: If I failed Capstone I in the Fall 2024, can I redo it in Spring 2025?  
### Answer: 

If you failed Capstone I in the Fall 2024, you typically cannot simply retake it in the Spring 2025. Generally, the Capstone sequence follows a specific timeline where Capstone I is completed in the Fall and Capstone II in the following Spring. If you fail Capstone I, you would need to reapply and meet all the eligibility criteria again for the next Capstone cycle, which would likely be in Fall 2025. Additionally, you would need to ensure you meet the GPA requirement of 3.2 throughout your senior year to be eligible for an Honors designation. Please refer to the specific guidelines provided in the History Capstone Handbook, AY2025-26, for more detailed information. The handbook outlines the process and timelines for applying to the Capstone program, including how to proceed if you do not initially succeed.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: VIETNAM STUDIES CAPSTONE GUIDELINES.pdf, Page: 6]
complete by the beginning of Capstone I • No outstanding Incompletes at the time of application. Capstone applicants will be assessed by the major faculty based on the eligibility criteria and the quality of the proposal. NOTE: Successful Capstone applicants must maintain a 3.2 GPA throughout their senior year to be able to earn an Honors for the Capstone. Failure to maintain the required GPA will result in the Capstone being capped at Pass. 1.2. Allocation of advisor process Successful applicants will be matched to their ﬁrst choice of primary and secondary advisor where possible. If the student’s ﬁrst or second preference cannot be accommodated due to the necessity of maintaining a fair distribution of faculty workload, the major Capstone coordinator will consult with the student to determine an appropriate solution. 1.3. seminars you have completed) and want an opportunity to carry out a long-term research project. For such students, the Capstone year provides time and guidance that is unparalleled by any course or other opportunity at the undergraduate level. However, if you wish to graduate with distinction—an honorable goal— but you don’t particularly enjoy doing independent research, you may want to skip the Capstone and focus on GPA honors instead! Normally, the Capstone sequence begins in the Fall with Capstone I and ends in the Spring with Capstone II. It culminates with a formal defense and a final evaluation by two readers. Students work with a primary advisor and, to a lesser extent, a secondary advisor. The format and length of projects is flexible, within certain limits. This handbook explains each aspect of the Capstone experience so that you can plan ahead and know what to expect. 1.2. History Capstone Learning Outcomes Students who successfully complete a Capstone project will be able to: 1. Demonstrate

the project and/or its suspension. For this reason, we advise students to begin their IRB application as soon as their Capstone application is accepted, or during Capstone I (preferably week 3) at the latest. In any case, students should have their questionnaire ready and approved at the end of Capstone I. More information on the IRB approval process can be found at https://fulbright.edu.vn/irb/ 1.11. Academic Integrity The capstone is subject to the regulations described in Fulbright University Vietnam’s Code of Academic Integrity including the use of generative AI. Presenting text, images, or other content created by others or by generative AI as your own work, even at the sentence, is grounds for failure of Capstone I and/or Capstone II. ### Question 25: If I do Literature capstone in Decolonial studies, can it be approved?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided, a capstone project in Decolonial studies may not be approved if there is no faculty expertise in that field. The context states that "Projects for which there is no faculty expertise may not be approved." Therefore, for a Literature capstone in Decolonial studies to be approved, there would need to be a faculty member with expertise in Decolonial studies. Since this is not specified in the given information, it is likely that such a project would not be approved. However, it's always advisable to consult with a prospective advisor early in the junior year to determine the suitability and feasibility of the proposed project.

### Question 27: Can Discrete Mathematics be counted for both Computer Science and Applied Mathematics majors?  
### Answer: 

No, Discrete Mathematics cannot be counted for both Computer Science and Applied Mathematics majors. The context states that students may not double count a course for two different requirements. Therefore, MATH 202 - Discrete Math can only count for either the Computer Science major or the Applied Mathematics major, but not both.

### Question 28: What steps should I take to ensure a smooth transfer of my exchange semester credits from Bard College to Fulbright?  
### Answer: 

To ensure a smooth transfer of your exchange semester credits from Bard College to Fulbright, you should follow these steps:

1. Review the Transfer Credit Policy V1.0 published in the One-Stop portal to understand Fulbright's policies and procedures.

2. Gather all necessary documentation, including an official transcript with seal from Bard College, and send it directly to the Office of the Registrar at the specified email or mailing address.

3. Complete and submit the Application for Credit Transfer form, ensuring that you provide all the requested information about the courses for which you are applying to transfer. This information may include the course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments.

4. Consult with your Academic/Major Advisor about your program plan to ensure that the courses you are transferring meet the requirements for your Fulbright degree.

5. Submit your completed application and supporting documents to the Office of the Registrar.

6. Allow sufficient time for the Office of the Registrar to review your application and coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine whether credit or an exemption is justified.

7. Monitor the status of your application through the One Stop portal and communicate with the Office of the Registrar if you have any questions or concerns. 

By following these steps, you can help ensure a smooth transfer of your exchange semester credits from Bard College to Fulbright. Remember that Fulbright will not evaluate transferable credit prior to acceptance, so make sure to complete these steps after you have been accepted into the Fulbright program.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]

Information may include but not limited to course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments. To apply for Credit Transfer or an Exemption, students should submit an Application for Credit Transfer, along with the required information on the course(s), to the Office of the Registrar. The Registrar will coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine whether credit or an exemption is justified. ### Question 29: Are 100-level and 200-level courses that are not explicitly categorized as E1, E2, E3, or E4 also excluded from fulfilling the Exploratory requirement?  
### Answer: 

Yes, 100-level and 200-level courses that are not explicitly categorized as E1, E2, E3, or E4 are also excluded from fulfilling the Exploratory requirement. According to the context provided, students need to complete 8 credits (2 courses at the 100-level or 200-level) chosen from each of the three categories: E1- Arts and Humanities, E2-Social Sciences, and STEM. This implies that only courses explicitly categorized under these three categories are eligible for fulfilling the Exploratory requirement. Courses not categorized as such do not count towards this requirement.

### Question 30: I am a Co25 student pursuing a Computer Science major, can I choose to follow either the old flowchart or the new one?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided, it appears that there are two different plans outlined - an "old" plan and a "new" plan. The old plan is described in the first part of the text, while the new plan is described in the second part. As a Co25 student pursuing a Computer Science major, you would need to follow the new plan, as it is the current curriculum structure. The old plan is no longer applicable. Therefore, you cannot choose to follow the old flowchart; you must follow the new one.

CS302: Algorithms & Theory of Computing Prerequisites: CS201 & MATH 202 Are there any eﬀicient algorithms to ﬁnd the shortest path between two cities on a map, schedule courses at FUV, or detect if a computer program is a virus or not? This Algorithms and Theory of Computing course aims to provide students with concepts and techniques to address these questions. Three common techniques (divide-and-conquer, greedy, and dynamic programming) and some algorithms on graphs are introduced to help students learn how to design eﬀicient algorithms for problems in practice. Students will also learn basic computational models (ﬁnite automaton, push- down

[Source: CS_major_handbook.pdf, Page: 19]
Furthermore, advanced topics such as meta- programming and program synthesis are also discussed, enabling students to envision the evolving landscape of programming languages in the future. CS301: Foundations of Software Engineering Prerequisites: CS207 Large scale systems, including web-based applications, are fundamentally diﬀerent and more complex than short programs. Software engineering is the study of how to develop large-scale software systems. In this course, students will learn about and practice a variety of interrelated activities and processes, including requirements analysis, system design, documentation, implementation, and testing. Students will also participate in and contribute to a major software project. Projects might vary from year to year depending on student and faculty interests, and could include mobile, web, game, or embedded systems. ### Question 31: If I withdraw from a course after the 4th week of the semester, will I be deducted 4 credits of financial aid?  
### Answer: 

No, you will not be deducted 4 credits of financial aid. Withdrawing from a course after the 4th week of the semester will result in a grade of 'F', which affects your GPA. However, it does not automatically lead to a deduction in financial aid credits as long as you maintain a minimum of 12 academic credits. Financial aid eligibility is affected if your course withdrawal results in fewer than the minimum credits for full-time enrollment.

Exceptions will only be permitted in exceptional circumstances (see Section 12), and it requires supporting documentation as well as the authorization of course instructor(s), the student’s academic/major advisor, and the Registrar’s Office. ### Question 32: Why do I need to take 8 exploratory courses?  
### Answer: 

You need to take 8 exploratory courses to step out of your comfort zone and explore broad areas of study. This helps you discover more fully where your interests and passions lie. These courses are designed to cover three main categories: E1- Arts and Humanities, E2-Social Sciences, and STEM. Each category requires 2 courses at the 100-level or 200-level, totaling 8 credits. No single course can fulfill more than one category. Additionally, up to 8 exploratory credits can be taken as Pass/No Pass, and up to two of these credits can count towards your major requirements. The goal is for students to complete these requirements by the end of their second year. However, it's important to note that class of 2023 students are exempted from this requirement. For classes of 2024, 2025, 2026, and 2027, there are four specific categories, and different credit requirements apply.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]

No course can be taken to fulfill more than one category. At most, 8 exploratory credits can be taken as Pass/No Pass. Up to two 8 exploratory credits (2 courses) can be counted towards the student’s major requirements. If a student has more than one major, the 8-credit limit is independently applied to each major. Students should aim to complete the Exploratory requirements by the end of their second year. ### Question 33: Can I take 160 credits in 4 years given that I pay for the full tuition fee?  
### Answer: 

No, you cannot take 160 credits in 4 years. According to the context provided, a typical full-time course load is 16 credit hours per term, which means a full-time student would take 64 credit hours per year (16 credit hours/term * 4 terms/year). Therefore, over four years, a full-time student would accumulate 256 credit hours, not 160. Additionally, to graduate with an undergraduate degree from Fulbright, a student must earn a minimum of 128 credit hours. So, it is not feasible to take 160 credits in 4 years under these conditions. Moreover, the maximum number of credit hours that can be transferred and credited to a Fulbright undergraduate degree is 64 credit hours, meaning you cannot exceed this limit even if you attend for more than the required number of years. Hence, you would need to adjust your course load to comply with the institution's policies and requirements. Paying for full tuition fees does not change these academic regulations.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 7]
with an undergraduate degree from Fulbright, a student must earn a minimum of 128 credit hours.  The typical full-time course load is 16 credit hours per term or 4 courses of 4 credit hours each. In order to make standard progress toward completing the degree, students are required to register for no fewer than 12 credit hours and no more than 20 credit hours per term. Students who wish to take fewer than 12 or more than 16 credit hours in one term must submit the Petition for Alternative Course Load or Maximum Course Load Request form to the Registrar's Office. The request form must be approved and signed by the Academic/Major Advisor before submission. STUDENT ENROLLMENT: 3.1 Course Load and Credit Hours Fulbright University Vietnam uses the “credit hour” as the quantum for course workload in the undergraduate program. A credit hour typically represents 3 hours of work during each week of a 16-week term. For a 4- credit hour course, a student would, therefore, be expected to put in 12 hours of work per week, including class time, for a total of 192 hours of work during a term. There are earned credits and attempted credits. Earned credits refer to the number of credit hours a student successfully completes with a grade of D or higher for letter grade options and a Pass for Pass/No Pass options. Attempted credits are the credit hours students enroll in and are recorded in the transcript, regardless of whether they complete the courses or pass them. This includes all courses for which a student receives a grade, including withdrawals (W), incompletes (I), repeats (RP), and failures (F). See section 4 for more details on different types of grades. To graduate

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
their Fulbright undergraduate degree. This is referred to as Credit Transfer. In addition, a student who has credit for a course passed at another university that is evaluated to be equivalent to a course at Fulbright may be given an Exemption from being required to do that Fulbright course. A maximum of 64 credit hours can be transferred and credited to a Fulbright undergraduate degree. That is, to earn a Fulbright University Vietnam undergraduate degree, a student must earn at least 64 credit hours from courses delivered by Fulbright. When applying for Credit Transfer, a student is responsible for providing all the information that is requested about the course(s) for which they are applying to transfer. Information may include but not limited to course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments. To apply for Credit Transfer or an Exemption, students should submit an Application for Credit Transfer, along with the required information on the course(s), to the Office of the Registrar.

### Question 34: What are the requirements for mathematics courses to pursue Human-Centered Engineering major?  
### Answer: 

To pursue the Human-Centered Engineering major, students need to take at least one Pure Mathematics course and at least two Advanced courses. They should also consider taking Elective courses in Arts, Humanities, Social Sciences, and Entrepreneurship as part of a human-centered approach. Additionally, students might need to take Foundation Engineering courses and Engineering Advanced courses once they declare their major or minor in Engineering. The specific requirements for Applied Mathematics courses include taking at least two Applied courses, at least one at the 200 level, and consulting with an academic advisor for course selection. Pure Mathematics courses provide essential abstract concepts and structures connecting various branches of Mathematics, helping students understand the adaptability of Mathematics to different types of problems. Advanced courses cover topics like Advanced Statistics, Statistical Learning, Stochastic Calculus, Numerical Analysis, Optimization, and Partial Differential Equations. Students must ensure they do not double-count a course for two different requirements. The Capstone project is optional and involves completing a one-year-long research project in the last year of study, resulting in either a research paper or a product contributing to the knowledge of mathematics or its applications. The Foundation Engineering courses aim to expose students to understanding user needs, defining engineering problems, and ideating potential solutions before gaining hands-on experience creating, making, and testing physical products. These courses are accessible to undetermined-major students and can be pursued alongside other courses of interest. Once the major or minor is declared, students will gain more specialized knowledge and skills through Engineering Foundation and Engineering Advanced courses. The Optimization and Partial Differential Equations Elective Applied courses are examples of courses that emphasize the applications of Mathematics and can be taken to fulfill the requirement. Students should check prerequisites and obtain instructor's approval if necessary. The Economics and Engineering Courses listed are examples of Applied courses that can be taken to meet the requirement. The Computer Science Courses listed are examples of courses that can be taken to meet the requirement. The Applied Mathematics Courses listed are examples of courses that can be taken to meet the requirement. The Pure Mathematics Courses listed are examples of courses that can be taken to meet the requirement. The Research Seminars provide opportunities for students to understand faculty's research and recent developments in mathematical research, practicing basic research skills. The Capstone project is an optional one-year-long research project to be completed in the last year of study, resulting in either a research paper or a product which contributes to the knowledge of mathematics or its applications. The requirements for declaring the Applied Mathematics Major include taking at least one Pure Mathematics course and at least two Advanced courses. Students should consult with an academic advisor for course selection. The Capstone project is optional and involves completing a one-year-long research project in the last year of study, resulting in either a research paper or a product which contributes to the knowledge of mathematics or its applications. The requirements for pursuing the Human-Centered Engineering major include taking Foundation Engineering courses, Engineering Advanced courses, and Elective courses in Arts, Humanities, Social Sciences, and Entrepreneurship. Students should also take at least one Pure Mathematics course and at least two Advanced courses. The specific requirements for Applied Mathematics courses include taking at least two Applied courses, at least one at the 200 level, and consulting with an academic advisor for course selection. ### Question 35: How is the grade of a replaced course displayed on the transcript? Will it replace the old one or create a new entry in the transcript?  
### Answer: 

The grade of a replaced course is displayed on the transcript such that the lower grade is overwritten by the notation "RP", meaning "repeated", and remains on the transcript. The higher grade is kept and used in the GPA calculation. Therefore, the replaced course does not create a new entry but rather updates the existing record with the "RP" notation.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
advisor, the course instructor, and the Registrar’s Office. Considerations will include course availability and capacity in the next academic term or next academic year. A higher grade will be kept and used in the GPA calculation. The lower grade will be overwritten by the notation “RP”, meaning “repeated”, and remain on the transcript. Credits of the repeated course are counted toward the total attempted credits. A student may not retake the same course for the third time unless he/she failed the second time or if a specific grade is needed to meet the major requirements. ### Question 36: What are the courses that can replace the capstone for a given major?  
### Answer: 

For a given major, students who choose not to do a capstone can replace it with 8 credits from IS courses, including at least 4 credits of 300-level course(s). This applies specifically to the Integrated Sciences (IS) major at Fulbright University Vietnam (FUV). Other majors may have different requirements for replacing the capstone. Please consult with program coordinators and potential advisors to determine the specific options available for your major.

### Question 37: Is it possible to graduate with double majors in Human-Centered Engineering and Applied Mathematics? If yes, please provide a sample study plan.  
### Answer: 

Yes, it is possible to graduate with double majors in Human-Centered Engineering and Applied Mathematics. However, the provided text does not give specific details on how to structure a study plan for this scenario. 

A sample study plan could look like this:

1. First two years:
   - Complete foundational courses in both Human-Centered Engineering and Applied Mathematics.

2. Third year:
   - Take Engineering Foundation courses in Human-Centered Engineering.
   - Take Pure Mathematics courses in Applied Mathematics.

3. Fourth year:
   - Take Engineering Advanced courses in Human-Centered Engineering.
   - Take Advanced courses in Applied Mathematics.

4. Fifth year:
   - Take Elective courses in Arts, Humanities, and Social Sciences in Human-Centered Engineering.
   - Take Elective Applied courses in Applied Mathematics.

5. Sixth year:
   - Complete remaining courses in both majors, including Research seminars and possibly a thesis or project.

Please note that this is just a general outline and actual course selection should be done in consultation with an academic advisor. Also, students must ensure that they do not double count courses for two different requirements. For example, Operations research can only count for either 1 Advanced course or 1 Elective course, but not both. This plan assumes that the student has already declared their majors and minors in Engineering and Applied Mathematics respectively. If not, they would first need to declare these before proceeding with the plan. The exact courses and sequence might vary depending on the institution and the specific requirements of each major. 

Career Path: After graduation, the student may choose different career options such as starting-up their own companies, working in industry or enrolling into post-graduate programs. The following table describes the path for different tracks. Fresh Graduate 3-5 years 10 years and above Engineer (Hardware/ Software) Senior Engineer Expert, e.g., senior engineer and/or Chief Technology Officer (CTO) role Product Development Engineer Project/ Product Team leader Senior Director or C-level executives Enroll in international postgraduate programs Graduated Master, change to management track or continue research track to obtain a Ph.D. degree Tenured faculty, leading researcher at top universities. 

This plan provides a broad overview and does not include specific course names or numbers, which would depend on the particular institutions and programs involved. It also assumes that the student has already declared their majors and minors in Engineering and Applied Mathematics respectively. If not, they would first need to declare these before proceeding with the plan. The exact courses and sequence might vary depending on the institution and the specific requirements of each major.

### Question 39: What are the exchange policies of Fulbright?  
### Answer: 

The exchange policies of Fulbright are not explicitly detailed in the provided text. However, it mentions that students can apply for Credit Transfer or an Exemption by submitting an Application for Credit Transfer along with required information about the course(s) to the Office of the Registrar. The decision on whether credit or an exemption is justified is coordinated with the Office of the Dean. It also notes that Credit Transfer from A-level, Advanced Placement (AP), International Baccalaureate (IB), and Cambridge International Exam (CIE) courses will be determined according to the AP/IB/CIE Credit Policy (in development). For more detailed information, one should refer to the Transfer Credit policy_Final_V3.0 published in the One Stop portal. There is no mention of general exchange policies beyond these specific instances.

### Question 40: What actions are considered plagiarism? Are AI-generated works counted?  
### Answer: 

Presenting text, images, or other content created by others or by generative AI as your own work, even at the sentence level, is considered plagiarism and grounds for failure of Capstone I and/or Capstone II. Yes, AI-generated works are counted and must be fully documented according to the guidelines provided.

Academic Integrity The Capstone is subject to the regulations described in Fulbright University Vietnam’s Code of Academic Integrity, including updates on usage of generative AI. Creative projects involving generative AI will require full documentation of its usage. Creative projects that incorporate generative AI must include comprehensive documentation covering every aspect of AI usage. This documentation should include: • Objective and Scope: Clearly deﬁne the reasons for utilizing generative AI and the speciﬁc elements of the project it contributes to. • Tools and Platforms: Specify the AI tools, models, or platforms employed. • Process and Methodology: Outline how AI will be incorporated, detailing which aspects of the project will be generated, improved, or altered with the use of AI. • Ethical and Copyright Issues: Address the ethical and copyright concerns associated with using generative AI and how these will be addressed throughout

### Question 41: Why is the graduation requirement 128 credits, but the major requirement is only 48 credits?  
### Answer: 

The graduation requirement is 128 credits because it includes all the institutional requirements, which go beyond just the major requirements. The major requirement being only 48 credits refers specifically to the courses needed to complete a single major, but the overall graduation requirement encompasses a broader curriculum including general education courses, electives, and possibly other requirements such as those for minors or special programs. Therefore, the 128 credit total is necessary to ensure students receive a well-rounded education covering various disciplines and areas of study.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
major or minor requirements must be taken for a letter grade. Students can claim a maximum of 8 credits (2 courses) toward both their Exploratory and major requirements. During their final year of study, students have the option to either complete a capstone project, which will count for 8 credits in their major area of study, or fulfill those credits with additional advanced coursework. Students pursuing a double major must complete all requirements for each major. If two majors (or two minors, or a major and a minor) share cross- listed or tagged1 courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. This limit is per each pair of majors (or major and minor) and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. For example, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. This rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or

### Question 42: Explain the cross-listed mechanism between courses.  
### Answer: 

The cross-listed mechanism allows students to use up to 8 credits (two courses) from a pair of majors or a major and a minor to satisfy both sets of requirements. This limit applies per each pair of majors or major and minor and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. However, this rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or tagged. For instance, if major A requires certain courses from major B for out-of-area foundation, exploration, or applications of the major, and these courses are not cross-listed between A and B, they do not count toward the 8-credit limit. Additionally, in interdisciplinary minors, the requirements mainly consist of courses from other majors, which are usually not cross-listed with the minors and are referred to as 'tagged' by these minors. These tagged courses also do not count towards the 8-credit limit. The cross-listed mechanism aims to provide flexibility for students to fulfill their major and minor requirements while taking advantage of courses offered in different departments.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
and a minor) share cross- listed or tagged1 courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. This limit is per each pair of majors (or major and minor) and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. For example, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. This rule does not apply to courses that are not cross-listed or tagged. ### Question 44: How does the core quest course selection work to fulfill core credits?  
### Answer: 

To fulfill core credits, students select one course from the QUEST (Quantitative Understanding and Empirical Scientific Thinking) core group, which consists of four courses: Quantitative Reasoning for a Digital Age (4 credits), Scientific Inquiry (4 credits), Introduction to Statistics (4 credits), and Programming for Data Science and Visualization (4 credits). These courses are pre-assigned to students during their first year or the first semester of their second year. The selection of one course from this group helps meet the core curriculum requirement for quantitative understanding and empirical scientific thinking.

### Question 45: Can I take a 300-level course to fulfill a 200-level major requirement?  
### Answer: 

No, you cannot take a 300-level course to fulfill a 200-level major requirement. The context specifies that for the major, students are required to take six (06) 200-level intermediate courses and four (04) 300-level advanced courses. Therefore, 300-level courses cannot be used to fulfill the 200-level requirement.

### Question 46: If I take a course at another university and want to transfer the credits to Fulbright, but Fulbright doesn’t have that major code, yet the course is related to a major at Fulbright, can I count it toward that major?  
### Answer: 

No, you cannot count the course toward that major at Fulbright if Fulbright doesn't have that major code. The context states that only courses from Fulbright can be used to fulfill major or minor requirements. Therefore, a course from another university that does not have a corresponding major code at Fulbright cannot be counted toward that major. However, you might be able to apply for a Credit Transfer or an Exemption if the course is evaluated to be equivalent to a Fulbright course. But it would still need to be coordinated with the Office of the Dean to determine justification.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]

Students shall consult with their Academic/Major Advisor about their program plan if they are considering taking the class for a third time. 4.2 Final Grade Release Final grades will be posted by the Registrar’s Office and accessible via the One Stop portal. 4.3 Credit Transfer and Exemptions earned from other universities. A student who has earned credit at another school or university may apply to have that credit counted towards their Fulbright undergraduate degree. This is referred to as Credit Transfer. In addition, a student who has credit for a course passed at another university that is evaluated to be equivalent to a course at Fulbright may be given an Exemption from being required to do that Fulbright course. That is, to earn a Fulbright University Vietnam undergraduate degree, a student must earn at least 64 credit hours from

Information may include but not limited to course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments. To apply for Credit Transfer or an Exemption, students should submit an Application for Credit Transfer, along with the required information on the course(s), to the Office of the Registrar. The Registrar will coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine whether credit or an exemption is justified. ### Question 47: I have 112 credits from Fulbright and 16 credits from EL. Can I graduate?  
### Answer: 

No, you cannot graduate. According to the information provided, to earn a Fulbright University Vietnam undergraduate degree, a student must earn at least 128 credit hours from Fulbright. You currently have 112 credits from Fulbright and 16 credits from EL, totaling 128 credits. However, since the requirement specifies that at least 64 credit hours must be earned from Fulbright, and you have only 112 credits from Fulbright, you are short of the required 64 credits. Therefore, you need additional credits from Fulbright to meet the graduation requirement.

### Question 48: I have received an offer to attend an international conference but lack funding. What school funds can I apply for?  
### Answer: 

You can apply for funding from Fulbright University's student research fund, which supports student's research projects, including capstone. This fund might be applicable for attending an international conference if it aligns with your research or academic goals. Additionally, you could explore applying for funding from other external sources. It's advisable to consult with your advisor to discuss potential changes to your experimental design if necessary.

[Source: Psychology Capstone Handbook 2025-2026.pdf, Page: 24]

### Question 49: What is the maximum number of credits I can transfer from another university after officially enrolling at Fulbright?  
### Answer: 

The maximum number of credits you can transfer from another university after officially enrolling at Fulbright is 64 credit hours. This means that to earn a Fulbright University Vietnam undergraduate degree, you must earn at least 64 credit hours from courses delivered by Fulbright itself. However, keep in mind that you need a total of 128 credit hours to graduate with an undergraduate degree from Fulbright. The remaining 64 credit hours must be earned through courses offered by Fulbright.

In addition, a student who has credit for a course passed at another university that is evaluated to be equivalent to a course at Fulbright may be given an Exemption from being required to do that Fulbright course. A maximum of 64 credit hours can be transferred and credited to a Fulbright undergraduate degree. That is, to earn a Fulbright University Vietnam undergraduate degree, a student must earn at least 64 credit hours from courses delivered by Fulbright. ### Question 50: In a regular semester, can I take only 2 courses? If so, how will my tuition fees be affected?  
### Answer: 

In a regular semester, taking only 2 courses would mean you are taking fewer than the minimum 12 credit hours required for full-time enrollment status. According to the information provided, no reduction in tuition is granted to students whose course withdrawal results in fewer than 12 academic credits. Therefore, your tuition fees will not be reduced if you take only 2 courses. However, it's important to note that taking fewer than 12 credit hours might affect your financial aid eligibility. It's advisable to consult the "Fees & Charges Guide" for undergraduate students for detailed information regarding tuition and financial aid. Additionally, if you wish to take fewer than 12 credit hours, you need to submit the Petition for Alternative Course Load form to the Registrar's Office, which must be approved by your Academic/Major Advisor.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 7]

The first period starts after 4:00 PM Friday, Week 2 to 4:00 PM Friday, Week 4. During this time, students can request to withdraw from the course without any consequence. The second period starts after 4:00 PM Friday, Week 4 to 4:00 PM Friday, Week 8. Attempted credits and a “W” grade will be recorded on the transcript for the course(s) from which students withdraw in this period. This grade does not affect a student’s GPA. In order to withdraw from a course, students need to submit the Course Withdrawal form to the Registrar’s Office, following the above timeline. ### Question 51: Can I pursue 3 majors?  
### Answer: 

According to the information provided, you can't directly pursue 3 majors. The text specifies that "Students pursuing a double major must complete all requirements for each major." This implies that pursuing more than two majors would require each additional major to also meet all its specific requirements, which is not explicitly addressed in the given context. Therefore, while it's possible to have multiple minors or a combination of a major and a minor, pursuing three distinct majors simultaneously isn't mentioned as a feasible option within the described framework. It's advisable to consult the academic advisor for confirmation on this point.

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 20]
major or minor requirements must be taken for a letter grade. Students can claim a maximum of 8 credits (2 courses) toward both their Exploratory and major requirements. During their final year of study, students have the option to either complete a capstone project, which will count for 8 credits in their major area of study, or fulfill those credits with additional advanced coursework. Students pursuing a double major must complete all requirements for each major. If two majors (or two minors, or a major and a minor) share cross- listed or tagged1 courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. ### Question 52: How can I change my major declaration?  
### Answer: 

To change your major declaration, you would typically need to follow the specific procedures outlined by your institution's academic advising office or the Dean's Office. This often involves submitting a formal petition or request form, which may require approval from both the major coordinator and the Dean's Office. It's important to check the specific policies related to major changes within the Social Studies Major and Minor or any other major you're interested in, as these can vary. Additionally, ensure you meet any specific requirements or conditions set forth for changing your major. Always coordinate with a supervisor or advisor during this process to ensure compliance with all necessary steps and requirements.

### Question 53: What is the process of delaying my payment?  
### Answer: 

The process of requesting a delay in your payment involves contacting Student Financial Services to request a late and/or an extension of tuition fee payment. They will try to understand the circumstances and ask for a timely response from you. During this period, you won't be able to register for new courses, participate in classes or a Work-Study Program. You can only return to active status once the outstanding balance is cleared. If you foresee difficulty in clearing the balance on time, it's advisable to meet with the Student Financial Services team early to discuss potential solutions. After the approved period of absence, if there's no response or registration in the returning term, you might be placed on Administrative Leave of Absence (Admin LOA) for a maximum of one term. If you're not registered or haven't confirmed your return within this term, you could be withdrawn from the program unless you've been granted an extension, which needs to be approved by both the Registrar’s Office and the Dean’s Office. Remember, the University recognizes that sometimes exceptional circumstances can arise, and these should be communicated promptly for consideration. Exceptions to this process include everyday issues like traffic congestion or missed buses, which do not qualify as exceptional circumstances. For such cases, students should directly contact the instructor at least two business days before the assessment due date. Evidence supporting the exceptional nature of the circumstances is often required. It's important to note that certain situations, such as loss of work not backed up or printing problems, do not qualify as exceptional circumstances. Always ensure that any claims of technical issues or other problems are supported by appropriate documentation.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 15]
Student Financial Services to request a late and/or an extension of tuition fee payment. Before placing a student in this type of absence, the Student Financial Services team will attempt to determine the circumstances and request a timely response from the student. With this absence status, students are unable to register for new course(s) during the registration period, participate in classes or a Work-Study Program in the current term. A student will only be reinstated as “Active” status if the outstanding balance is clear. If the student anticipates being unable to clear the account on time, the student should meet with the Student Financial Services team as soon as possible to request assistance and alternative solutions. After the approved period of absence, a student is put on Administrative Leave of Absence (Admin LOA) for a maximum of one term if the Registrar’s Office receives no response of return confirmation or no registration in the returning term. ### Question 54: Which major has the fewest requirements?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided, the major with the fewest requirements appears to be Computer Science. It requires a total of 56 credits, including foundational courses, intermediate courses, advanced courses, and capstone projects. While other majors like Engineering and Applied Mathematics also require specific courses, the details for those majors suggest they might have more total credit hours or additional requirements. Therefore, Computer Science seems to have the fewest requirements among the mentioned majors. However, without specific credit hour comparisons for all potential majors, this conclusion is based on the provided data. Other majors might have different structures or additional requirements not detailed here.

### Question 55: How many courses can I take in total?  
### Answer: 

You can take a maximum of 8 credits (2 courses) toward both your Exploratory and major requirements combined. Additionally, you can take up to 8 credits (2 courses) as Pass/No Pass towards your major requirements. If you have more than one major, the 8-credit limit is independently applied to each major. Therefore, the total number of courses you can take in total depends on your specific requirements and how you choose to allocate your credits between exploratory studies, major requirements, and electives. However, there is no explicit limit mentioned for the total number of courses you can take overall. It's important to note that the number of elective credits may vary, but the total number of earned credits must meet the degree requirements.

### Question 56: How many courses in a semester can I take in total?  
### Answer: 

You can take a total of 16 to 20 courses in a semester, depending on your course load. Typically, a full-time course load is 4 courses of 4 credit hours each, which totals 16 credit hours. However, you can take up to 20 credit hours per term if approved by the Academic/Major Advisor through the Petition for Alternative Course Load or Maximum Course Load Request form. If you wish to take fewer than 12 credit hours, you must also submit a petition and get approval. It's important to note that students on a Leave of Absence are still considered enrolled but not registered for any courses. During the leave period, they are not allowed to join other official university activities.

STUDENT ENROLLMENT: 3.1 Course Load and Credit Hours Fulbright University Vietnam uses the “credit hour” as the quantum for course workload in the undergraduate program. A credit hour typically represents 3 hours of work during each week of a 16-week term. For a 4- credit hour course, a student would, therefore, be expected to put in 12 hours of work per week, including class time, for a total of 192 hours of work during a term. There are earned credits and attempted credits. Earned credits refer to the number of credit hours a student successfully completes with a grade of D or higher for letter grade options and a Pass for Pass/No Pass options. Attempted credits are the credit hours students enroll in and are recorded in the transcript, regardless of whether they complete the courses or pass them. This includes all courses for which a student receives a grade, including withdrawals (W), incompletes (I), repeats (RP), and failures (F). See section 4 for more details on different types of grades. To graduate

[Source: CS_major_handbook.pdf, Page: 12]
limit is independently applied to each major. Students should aim to complete the Exploratory requirements by the end of their second year. APPEALS: A student who wishes to dispute a final grade in a course should first discuss the matter with the course instructor(s). If the matter remains unresolved and the student believes there has been an error in grading, bias, or failure to follow published grading policies, the student may file an appeal as follows: • Submit the Review of Final Grade Request form to the Registrar's Office within five (05) business days from the date on which the Registrar's Office posts the final grade for the term. • The Registrar's Office informs the Dean’s Office of the case. After investigation, if the Deans can mediate, no further action is required. Otherwise, the Registrar's Office organizes a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the grade. The grade determined after this evaluation shall be the final grade. In cases concerning the interpretation of a course policy, the Dean’s Office will defer to the course syllabus whenever possible and otherwise will make a final ruling on the

### Question 59: If I'm going for a double major then how many courses can be double count maximum?  
### Answer: 

If you're going for a double major, the maximum number of courses that can be double-counted is 8 credits (2 courses) per pair of majors. This means for two majors, you can double-count up to 8 credits. However, you must complete all requirements for each major. The rule about double-counting applies per pair of majors and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits across all your majors. So, for two majors, you can use up to 8 credits towards both sets of requirements.

### Question 60: Can you give me the grade translation from alphabetic to numerical?  
### Answer: 

The grade translation from alphabetic to numerical at Fulbright University Vietnam is as follows:

A - 4.0
B - 3.0
C - 2.0
D - 1.0
F - 0.0

Please note that 'C-' is the minimum passing grade for regular grading, but for Pass/No Pass grading, a 'C-' is required to pass or to be counted towards major/minor requirements or prerequisites. Grades 'D' or 'D+' can only be counted towards elective course requirements. The 'I' stands for Incomplete and 'W' stands for Withdrawal, which do not translate into numerical values for GPA calculations. The 'P' in P/NP stands for Pass and 'N' stands for No Pass, which also do not contribute to the GPA. The 'RP' stands for Repeat, which is not included in GPA calculations either.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 7]
GRADING: At Fulbright, the majority of courses apply a standard letter grade ranging from ‘A’ to ‘F.’ Grade points are assigned to letter grades according to the following scale (unless otherwise decided by faculty in individual courses): Letter Grade Grade Point Grade Category Percentage

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
o The Registrar’s Office is responsible for converting to the P/NP after receiving the final grade submission by the instructor at the end of the term. o A grade of ‘C-’ or higher will be counted as a Pass. Courses graded with a Pass grade can be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. o Any grade below a ‘C-’ will be counted as a No Pass. No credit is granted for this result. The NP grade will be shown on the Official Transcript. Courses with a NP grade cannot be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses. • I = Incomplete: If a student is unable to complete the work in a course because of illness, family emergency, or other exceptional circumstances (see Section 12), a temporary grade of ‘I’ (Incomplete) may be awarded by the faculty until unfinished course requirements are completed. The student has until the date agreed upon with the faculty (not to exceed 6 months from the end of the course) to complete all remaining course work; otherwise, the student will be

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
awarded a letter grade, which may be an ‘F’, based upon the work completed by the deadline. The student must fill out an Incomplete Grade Request form. The signed request form must be submitted no later than 4:00 PM to the Registrar’s Office, on the last day of the term end date. • W = Withdrawal: A grade of ‘W’ (Withdrawal) is issued for a student- initiated withdrawal after 4:00 PM Friday Week 4 and prior to the end of Week 8. A ‘W’ does not affect the student’s GPA. • Grade Point Average (GPA): GPA is calculated by dividing [the sum of (grade points earned * credit hours earned) for each course] by [the total attempted credits for GPA]. All courses for which a P/NP, I, W, or RP grade is awarded are excluded from the GPA calculation. • Grade Reports (Transcript): At the end of each term, grade reports are available for viewing on the Fulbright One Stop portal, named Unofficial Transcript. Paper copies of grade reports, named Transcript of Records, can be issued by the Registrar’s Office upon students’

### Question 62: Why and how am I getting academic suspension?  
### Answer: 

You are getting academic suspension because you failed to meet all the requirements of your Learning Contract while on Academic Probation. The process typically involves failing to attend an Academic Progress Meeting and not fulfilling the conditions set by the Learning Contract. Once these failures occur, you will be placed on Academic Suspension, which is entered on your transcript as part of your academic record. You must then meet with the Dean’s Office to establish the conditions you need to meet before returning to Fulbright. During the suspension period, you are not allowed to visit the Fulbright campus without permission from the Dean’s Office or the Vice President of Student Affairs for the purpose of attending relevant meetings. Suspensions are typically for one term or one academic year, and a student can be suspended a maximum of two times. If you are suspended a third time, your enrollment in the program will be canceled, and you will need to apply for re-admission, providing a letter explaining the reasons for your suspension and the measures you have taken to address those reasons. The re-admission decision is made by the Dean’s Office in consultation with the appropriate members of faculty and staff. Students who are re-admitted must also reapply for financial aid.

### Question 63: How does the P/NP grade work?  
### Answer: 

The P/NP (Pass/No Pass) grading system allows students to take up to 8 credits (usually 2 courses, each worth 4 credits) during an academic year under this option. To opt into this system, students need to submit a 'Petition to Elect Pass/No Pass Grade' form to the Registrar's Office before 4:00 PM on Friday of Week 4 of the term. 

Once a student opts for the P/NP system, they cannot revert back to the traditional letter grading system for those specific courses. Grades of 'C-' or higher are considered passes, meaning these courses can be used to meet prerequisites for future courses. Conversely, any grade below 'C-' results in a no pass (NP) grade, which does not provide any credit towards their degree requirements.

It's important to note that the P/NP system does not apply to core courses and cannot be used to fulfill major or minor requirements. Additionally, the Registrar's Office handles the conversion of final grades to either Pass or No Pass at the end of the term. This system provides flexibility for students who might want to focus on passing rather than achieving high letter grades, especially for less critical courses. However, it should be noted that grades of 'D' or 'D+' can only be counted towards elective course requirements. The final decision on whether a course is passed or not-passed is made based on the instructor's final grade submission. 

In summary, the P/NP system offers a way for students to manage their academic workload by focusing on passing courses without the pressure of earning high letter grades, but it comes with limitations regarding its application to certain types of courses and its impact on GPA calculations. Grades from P/NP courses are not included in the GPA computation.

### Question 64: How many courses can I take as P/NP at maximum and how will it contribute to the official transcript GPA?  
### Answer: 

You can take a maximum of 2 courses as P/NP, totaling 8 credits. These courses will not be included in the official transcript GPA calculation. Therefore, they do not contribute to the GPA. However, the 'P' grade will be shown on the Official Transcript. The 'NP' grade will also be shown on the Official Transcript but will not contribute to the GPA. The courses with a 'NP' grade cannot be used to meet prerequisite requirements for next-level courses.

### Question 65: I've failed the GWP due to personal reasons so will it count toward the 144 maximum credits I can have?  
### Answer: 

The information provided does not specify whether failing a course due to personal reasons affects the maximum number of credits a student can have. Typically, failing a course would count towards the total attempted credits. However, since you mentioned the GWP (likely referring to a Pass/No Pass system), grades from such courses are not included in the GPA calculation. Therefore, failing a course under the GWP system might not directly impact your maximum credit limit of 144 credits. It's best to consult with your Academic/Major Advisor for confirmation.

### Question 66: What and how do I get an Academic Warning?  
### Answer: 

To receive an Academic Warning, students who are not making satisfactory progress towards their degree and/or fall below a 2.0 GPA, or for other reasons such as failure of attendance, participation, citizenship, or academic integrity, will be notified by the Registrar’s Office. The student is then required to attend an Academic Progress Meeting where a Learning Contract will be created with specific conditions tailored to the individual situation. This is the first level of intervention aimed at students needing assistance to improve their academic standing. The Registrar's Office records this as a matter of file and follows up accordingly. If a student receives three official warnings, they will face Disciplinary Action, which could result in Academic Probation or Academic Suspension.
