### Question 68: Can you provide me with some courses suggestion to take to major in Math?  
### Answer: 

Based on the provided context, here are some suggested courses to major in Math:

**Foundation Courses (100 level):**
- Linear Algebra
- Single Variable Calculus
- Introduction to Statistics
- Multivariable Calculus

**Intermediate Courses (200 level):**
- Probability
- Differential Equations
- Discrete Mathematics
- Numerical Analysis

**Advanced Courses (300 level):**
- Advanced Statistics
- Statistical Learning
- Stochastic Calculus
- Numerical Analysis
- Optimization
- Partial Differential Equations

**Elective Applied Courses:**
- Game Theory (Sample Economics Course)
- Signal, Systems, and Control (Sample Engineering Course)
- Introduction to Machine Learning (Sample Computer Science Course)
- Operations Research (Sample Applied Mathematics Course)

**Pure Mathematics Courses:**
- Abstract Algebra
- Real Analysis

**Research Seminars:**
- Participate in research seminars to understand faculty's research and recent developments in mathematical research.

**Capstone Project (Optional):**
- Consider completing a capstone project for a deeper dive into a specific area of interest.

Remember to consult with an academic advisor for personalized course selection and to ensure that prerequisites are met. Also, note that students should not double-count courses for multiple requirements. For instance, Operations Research can only count as one Advanced Course or one Elective Course, but not both. 

This structured approach will help you build a strong foundation and specialization in your chosen area of applied mathematics. Good luck!

### Question 70: I'm currently under a General Work Program for Experiential Learning but the company do not pay me in any form. How can I get the subsidy from Fulbright University?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided in the context, there is no mention of subsidies for unpaid experiential learning programs. The Fulbright University's Experiential Learning Program (ELP) focuses on creating, standardizing, and facilitating academic credit-bearing experiential learning experiences, but it does not provide subsidies for companies that do not pay the student. Therefore, you would need to check with the relevant Fulbright University departments (Academic Affairs, Career Services, or Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation) to see if there are any other resources or support systems available for unpaid internships. However, it is important to note that the ELP primarily aims to ensure academic credit for your experiential learning activities rather than providing financial assistance for the internship itself.

All full-time, undergraduate, degree- seeking students must complete at least 04 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the ELP as a graduation requirement. ### Question 71: Can you give me the process of making a Capstone for graduation?  
### Answer: 

The process of making a Capstone for graduation involves several steps, starting from Capstone I in the Fall semester and concluding with Capstone II in the Spring semester. Here's a detailed breakdown:

1. **Capstone I (Fall Semester)**:
   - **Early Meetings**: Students meet with their advisors as soon as possible to set up a regular meeting schedule and establish expectations for submissions along with a timeline.
   - **Project Proposal and Research Questions**: Students revise their project proposal and/or research questions, often presenting them in the form of an introduction or prospectus.
   - **Close Readings**: Initial close readings are conducted.
   - **Field Journal Extracts**: For research projects, field journal extracts are provided.
   - **Creative Writing**: First drafts or excerpts of creative writing are submitted.

2. **Midterm Submission**:
   - Students submit revised project proposals and/or research questions, initial close readings, field journal extracts, and first drafts or excerpts of creative writing.

3. **End-of-Term Submission**:
   - Students prepare a literature review or annotated bibliography.
   - They also submit a sample chapter, introduction or preface, selections or excerpts of creative writing, or other relevant materials.

4. **Capstone II (Spring Semester)**:
   - **Focus on Production**: Students focus more on producing their final submission, whether it's writing or realizing an applied project.
   - **Research Participation**: Students participate in research in support of their final submission.
   - **Final Submission**: Students complete a written thesis and finish an applied project.
   - **Formal Presentation**: Students are encouraged to formally present their work at the end of Capstone II.
   - **Grading**: Capstone II is graded based on the student's final submission. Additionally, students are required to actively participate in advising activities and provide regular updates, including midterm submissions.

5. **Final Evaluation**: The Capstone sequence concludes with a formal defense and final evaluation by two readers. Students work closely with a primary advisor and a secondary advisor, depending on the flexibility of the project format and length.

Throughout this process, students receive guidance and feedback from their advisors to ensure they are on track to complete their Capstone projects successfully. The Capstone experience is designed to provide students with time and guidance that is unparalleled by any course or other opportunity at the undergraduate level. For those aiming to graduate with distinction, the Capstone process offers an excellent opportunity to engage in intensive research and produce a high-quality final submission. However, if students prefer to focus on GPA honors rather than independent research, they may choose to skip the Capstone.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Psychology Capstone Handbook 2025-2026.pdf, Page: 7]

### Question 72: What are the grades required to get a distinctive graduation?  
### Answer: 

The grades required to get a distinctive graduation, specifically "Graduation with Honors," according to the given text, are achieved by completing a capstone project that is graded as "Honors." Therefore, students need to successfully complete a capstone project graded as Honors to be awarded Graduation with Honors. There are no other specific grades mentioned for a distinctive graduation beyond this context.

opportunity to fulfill 8 credits of their major requirements via a capstone project. A student wishing to do a capstone must apply during the term prior to the first term of the capstone (Capstone I), and may only apply after having completed 80 credits of coursework. Students who do not do a capstone will need to fulfill 8 credits of coursework as specified in their major. Individual majors will determine eligibility requirements, and students should discuss their proposals with program coordinators and potential advisors to prepare their applications. Capstone projects will be graded No Pass/Pass/Honors and must be evaluated by the supervising faculty at least one month before the end of the student’s graduating term. ### Question 73: How can I graduate with Honor or lie within the top GPA?  
### Answer: 

To graduate with honors or maintain a high GPA, you need to meet specific criteria and requirements set by your major. For instance, in Computer Science, you must have a major GPA of 3.5 and maintain this GPA throughout your senior year. Similarly, for Social Studies, you need to maintain a 3.6 GPA. Failure to meet these GPA requirements will result in your capstone being capped at Pass instead of Honors. Additionally, completing a capstone project with a grade of "Honors" is another requirement for graduating with honors. It's important to discuss your capstone proposal with program coordinators and potential advisors to ensure you meet all the necessary criteria and maintain the required GPA. Regularly check your progress and seek feedback from your advisors to stay on track. Remember that each major may have its own specific requirements, so it's crucial to follow the guidelines provided by your respective department. Good luck!  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Major Descriptions and Flowcharts_OfficialVersion.pdf, Page: 76]
a grade of “honors” on their capstone.   Capstones provide students with the opportunity to work closely with an advisor to dive deeply into a topic of their interest with an emphasis on ethics, the application of theory to methods, and communication of their ideas.  While typical capstones will be research projects employing methods students have developed over the course of their studies, alternative projects such as films, social enterprises, policy reports, and digital media may also be developed in coordination with a supervisor. Requirements for Declaring the Social Studies Major and Minor In order to formally declare Social Studies as your major, you must complete Social Inquiry, and at least two courses at the 100 or 200 level.  In order to formally declare Social Studies minor, you must complete Social Inquiry and at least one course in the Social Studies Program. Graduation with Honors Requirements 1. ### Question 74: How many courses can I take with P/NP grade in total?  
### Answer: 

You can take a total of 2 courses with a P/NP grade in one academic year. Each course is typically 4 credits. Therefore, in total, you can take 8 credits worth of courses on a Pass/No Pass basis.

Students pursuing a double major must complete all requirements for each major. If two majors (or two minors, or a major and a minor) share cross- listed or tagged1 courses, up to 8 credits (two courses) can be used to satisfy both sets of requirements. This limit is per each pair of majors (or major and minor) and does not restrict the total number of double-counted credits or courses a student can claim. For example, a student can major in both A and B and minor in C with a total of 6 double-counted courses: two in A and B, two in B and C, and two in A and C. ### Question 75: How many types of absences are there?  
### Answer: 

There are four types of absences mentioned in the given text. They are general absences, excused absences due to university-sponsored events/activities, military leave, and excused absences for exceptional circumstances. However, the text also mentions that unplanned absences should be discussed with the course instructor(s) as soon as possible, implying that this could be considered a fifth type of absence. But since the text does not explicitly categorize it as a separate type, we can consider the four explicitly mentioned types as the answer. So, there are four types of absences.

### Question 76: How many types of leave of absence are there and how can I have one?  
### Answer: 

There are three types of leave of absence: personal leave, medical leave, and administrative leave of absence.

To have one, you need to follow specific procedures depending on the type of leave:

For personal or medical leave:
- Complete and submit the Undergraduate Leave of Absence form along with supporting documents.
- For medical leave, also submit the Fulbright Impact Assessment form and all medical supporting documents.
- Ensure you submit the request before the last day of class.
- The leave duration is determined in conjunction with the health services professional, the Registrar's Office, and the student.
- Indefinite leaves are not permitted.

For administrative leave of absence:
- You must have an outstanding student account balance in an enrolled term without informing Student Financial Services to request a late and/or an extension of tuition fee payment.
- Before placing you in this type of absence, the Student Financial Services team will attempt to determine the circumstances and request a timely response from you.

### Question 79: What is the school's policy on academic dishonesty, and how are violations handled?  
### Answer: 

The school's policy on academic dishonesty is outlined in Fulbright University Vietnam's Code of Academic Integrity. Violations of this code can lead to various consequences depending on the severity and frequency of the infractions. Typically, three official warnings result in more severe actions such as Academic Probation or Academic Suspension. Academic Probation serves as a second level of intervention aimed at alerting students about risks associated with their academic performance, potentially leading to temporary suspension or permanent dismissal if not addressed. Academic Suspension involves entering the suspension into the student's academic record and could indicate a temporary halt in studies due to unsatisfactory academic performance. These measures are designed to ensure academic integrity and uphold high standards within the educational institution.

### Question 80: What are the policies regarding retaking exams or improving grades?  
### Answer: 

The policies regarding retaking exams or improving grades are as follows:

1. Students are required to repeat core courses if they receive a grade of 'F' and/or courses counted toward major/minor if they receive a grade below 'C-'.
2. Students may also repeat a course if they have received a grade of 'D+', 'D', 'F', or NP for the course, or have withdrawn and received a grade of 'W'.
3. In special cases, a student may request to repeat a course after having received a grade higher than a 'D+' following consultation with the student's academic/major advisor, the course instructor, and the Registrar's Office.
4. A higher grade will be kept and used in the GPA calculation, while the lower grade will be overwritten by the notation "RP", meaning "repeated", and remain on the transcript.
5. Credits of the repeated course are counted toward the total attempted credits.
6. A student may not retake the same course for the third time unless they failed the second time or if a specific grade is needed to meet major requirements.
7. Students should consult with their Academic/Major Advisor about their program plan if they are considering taking the class for a third time.

### Question 81: How does the university accommodate students with chronic illnesses or personal emergencies that affect attendance?  
### Answer: 

The university accommodates students with chronic illnesses or personal emergencies that affect attendance by allowing them to apply for a medical leave of absence. Students must submit the Undergraduate Leave of Absence form, the Fulbright Impact Assessment form, and all medical supporting documents before the last day of class. The duration of the leave is determined in conjunction with the health services professional, the Registrar's Office, and the student. This process ensures that the student's recovery or safety is prioritized while providing necessary accommodations. For emergency cases where students cannot communicate their condition, the university considers these as exceptional circumstances and allows for excused absences. Additionally, students experiencing close bereavement or other exceptional circumstances can also seek accommodation through the appropriate forms and documentation. The instructors are expected to allow students to make up any missed assignments if the absence is reasonable and to inform students if they are in danger of failing the course due to class absence or missed assignments. The university encourages students to request permission to be absent and to contact their instructors to initiate arrangements to make up any missed work. However, it is important to note that everyday issues like traffic congestion or missed buses are not considered exceptional circumstances and do not warrant accommodation. The university also supports students participating in university-sponsored events and activities, provided they meet certain criteria and obtain the necessary approvals. Instructors are responsible for checking the student's academic standing with the Registrar's Office before approving such excused absences. Overall, the university aims to provide flexibility and support for students facing various challenges that may impact their attendance and academic performance.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 17]
EXCEPTIONAL CIRCUMSTANCES: The University acknowledges that sometimes a student will experience circumstances that will impact their ability to fulfill the expectations of the University, including but not limited to assessment, attendance, and paying fees. Housemates or very close friends may also be considered as ‘close’, though evidence of the relationship may be required. • Victim of a serious crime • Disabilities for which reasonable adjustments are not yet in place and where the delay is not due to the student • Exceptional and unforeseeable transport difficulties e.g., major transport incidents, cancelled flights. ### Question 82: Are students allowed to use AI tools like ChatGPT for assignments? If so, under what conditions?  
### Answer: 

Yes, students are allowed to use AI tools like ChatGPT for assignments, but under specific conditions. According to the provided context, creative projects involving generative AI, such as ChatGPT, require full documentation of its usage. This documentation should comprehensively cover various aspects of AI usage, including:

1. Objective and Scope: Clearly define the reasons for utilizing generative AI and the specific elements of the project it contributes to.
2. Tools and Platforms: Specify the AI tools, models, or platforms employed.
3. Process and Methodology: Outline how AI will be incorporated, detailing which aspects of the project will be generated, improved, or altered with the use of AI.
4. Ethical and Copyright Issues: Address the ethical and copyright concerns associated with using generative AI and how these will be addressed throughout the project.

This comprehensive documentation promotes transparency, offers insight into AI's role in the creative process, and highlights the originality and human contributions to the project. Therefore, students can use AI tools like ChatGPT for assignments, but they need to provide detailed documentation of their usage to meet academic integrity standards. Additionally, students must obtain IRB approval before beginning their Fulbright-affiliated research, which includes ensuring proper data protection and ethical considerations. They are advised to start this process as soon as their Capstone application is accepted or during Capstone I, preferably by week 7. More information on the IRB approval process can be found at the provided link.

### Question 83: Where can I get support for mental health treatment?  
### Answer: 

You can seek support for mental health treatment through various resources and services. One option is to participate in a Mental Health First Aid Training Program, which provides individuals with the skills to identify, understand, and respond to signs of mental illnesses and substance use disorders. Another option is to engage in a Community Survey on Mental Health Needs, which helps gather data on the prevalence and nature of mental health issues within a community, aiding in the development of targeted interventions. Additionally, a Public Art Project on Mental Health Themes can serve as a creative outlet and raise awareness about mental health issues. A Resource Guide for Local Mental Health Services can provide information on local clinics, therapists, and support groups. Lastly, a Therapeutic Gardening or Nature Program can offer a relaxing environment that promotes mental well-being. It's important to consult with professionals and explore these options to find the best fit for your needs. However, it's crucial to note that these projects are part of a Capstone by Applied Project and may not directly provide immediate mental health treatment. For immediate assistance, consider reaching out to a mental health professional or contacting local mental health organizations.

Fulbright’s Experiential Learning Program (ELP) exists to create, standardize, and facilitate academic credit-bearing experiential learning experiences. All full-time, undergraduate, degree- seeking students must complete at least 04 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the ELP as a graduation requirement. Current ELP streams are housed within Academic Affairs (AA), Career Services (CS), and Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation (CEI), where each team is responsible for administrative and academic duties of their respective stream(s). The ELP operates within Fulbright’s undergraduate program’s standard operating procedures and is developed in consultation with undergraduate program leadership and faculty. Regular communication with these offices can also help you stay informed about event schedules and plan your study times accordingly.

### Question 89: I used to take an undergraduate program at another university and I want to transfer credit of studied courses at that university. What should I do?  
### Answer: 

To transfer credit of studied courses from another university to your Fulbright undergraduate degree, you should follow these steps:

1. Gather all the required information about the course(s) for which you are applying to transfer. This includes the course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments.

2. Submit an Application for Credit Transfer, along with the required information on the course(s), to the Office of the Registrar.

3. The Registrar will coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine whether credit or an exemption is justified.

4. Keep in mind that a maximum of 64 credit hours can be transferred and credited to a Fulbright undergraduate degree. Therefore, ensure that you still meet the minimum requirement of earning at least 64 credit hours from courses delivered by Fulbright to earn your Fulbright University Vietnam undergraduate degree.

5. If you have any questions or need further assistance, consult with your Academic/Major Advisor.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
courses delivered by Fulbright. When applying for Credit Transfer, a student is responsible for providing all the information that is requested about the course(s) for which they are applying to transfer. Information may include but not limited to course curriculum, learning outcomes, course content, and assessments. To apply for Credit Transfer or an Exemption, students should submit an Application for Credit Transfer, along with the required information on the course(s), to the Office of the Registrar. The Registrar will coordinate with the Office of the Dean to determine whether credit or an exemption is justified. Credit Transfer from A-level, Advanced Placement (AP), International Baccalaureate (IB), and Cambridge International Exam (CIE) courses will be determined according to the AP/IB/CIE Credit Policy (in development). For more information, please refer to the Transfer Credit policy_Final_V3.0 published in the One Stop portal.

### Question 91: I'm a student athlete then how can I bypass all of physical education courses required to graduate?  
### Answer: 

As a student athlete, you cannot bypass the physical education courses required to graduate. According to the provided context, Physical Education courses are mandatory for all students, including those who are student athletes. These courses do not count toward the 128-credit requirement but are still necessary for graduation. Therefore, you would need to complete these courses as part of your graduation requirements. There is no mention of exceptions for student athletes regarding Physical Education courses.

• Physical Education • Political courses These courses do not count toward the 128-credit requirement. All students for whom English is not their first language must take an English Assessment Test required by NECHE Accreditation. 13.8  Double Counting In satisfying degree requirements, some courses can be double-counted. For example, an exploratory course can also be counted as a major course for the corresponding major. However, the number of double-counted credits is often limited (e.g., see subsections 13.2 and 13.3). Additionally, any particular course can only be used to satisfy at most two requirements. For instance, if course X is cross-listed between major A and major B and tagged by minor C, then X can be used to fulfill the requirements of major A and major B, or major A and minor C, or major B and minor C. Triple counting is not allowed. 13.9  Maximal Length of Study Fulbright follows MOET regulations, which state that the maximum time to complete the program cannot exceed double the standard

### Question 92: I'm currently a third year student and moved out of university dormitory after first year but now I'm struggling to find a new accommodation so can I register again for dormitory and will I still have the financial support?  
### Answer: 

Based on the information provided, it seems that you are asking about re-registering for dormitory accommodation and whether you would still receive financial support.

The context mentions that students on a Leave of Absence are considered still enrolled but not registered for any courses. However, this does not directly address your question about re-registering for dormitory accommodation or financial support.

To answer your question:
1. You would need to contact the Residential Life office to inquire about re-registering for dormitory accommodation. They will likely require you to fill out an application and provide documentation regarding your current living situation and reasons for needing dormitory accommodation.
2. Regarding financial support, you should contact the Student Financial Services team. They will assess your situation and determine if you qualify for financial aid or assistance. Your current financial balance and status as a third-year student might affect their decision.

It is recommended that you reach out to both the Residential Life office and the Student Financial Services team to discuss your specific circumstances and explore your options. They will be able to provide you with more detailed and personalized guidance.

### Question 94: How many ways are there provided by the university can I get the support in my academic path?  
### Answer: 

There are three main ways provided by the university to get support in your academic path:

1. Access to labs, tools, and software relevant to your project work.
2. Mentorship and Industry Involvement - Industry mentors may be available for project guidance, helping bridge academic learning and industry practice.
3. Limited funding for materials and resources for projects. 

These are the primary forms of support mentioned in the context provided. The university also acknowledges exceptional circumstances that may impact a student's ability to fulfill academic expectations, but these are not considered direct support mechanisms for the academic path. Additionally, logistical support is provided for projects that require arrangements outside the university's typical academic scope. However, this is not directly related to academic support. Therefore, the three main ways mentioned are the primary forms of support provided by the university for your academic path.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: HCE_Capstone_Handbook_Final_2025.01.16.pdf, Page: 9]

Mentorship and Industry Involvement Industry mentors may be available for project guidance, helping bridge academic learning and industry practice. They could be secondary advisors for Capstone projects, but not primary advisors or independent reviewers. They could also be invited to join the capstone panel. As either a secondary advisor or a member of the capstone panel, industry mentors could participate in grading. Funding and Material Procurement Projects will have access to limited funding for materials and resources. Policies on budgeting and purchasing will be provided.

### Question 97: I'm having some bad experience with a professor teaching a course. The problem was his way of delivering does not meet academic standard and I want to say something about this with people having higher authorities. What should I do?  
### Answer: 

According to the provided context, if you're experiencing issues with a professor's teaching methods and believe it doesn't meet academic standards, you should first address the matter with the course instructor. If the issue remains unresolved and you believe there has been an error in grading, bias, or a failure to follow published grading policies, you can then file an appeal. Specifically, you should submit the Review of Final Grade Request form to the Registrar's Office within five business days from the date the final grade is posted. The Registrar's Office will inform the Dean’s Office, which will investigate and potentially mediate the issue. If mediation is not sufficient, they will organize a panel review for an independent evaluation of the grade. This process aims to resolve disputes regarding grades and ensure adherence to established policies. However, it's important to note that the context does not specifically address concerns about teaching methods per se, but rather focuses on grading and policy adherence. For issues related to teaching methods, you might consider discussing these directly with the department chair or academic advisor for guidance on how to proceed.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]
APPEALS: A student who wishes to dispute a final grade in a course should first discuss the matter with the course instructor(s). If the matter remains unresolved and the student believes there has been an error in grading, bias, or failure to follow published grading policies, the student may file an appeal as follows: • Submit the Review of Final Grade Request form to the Registrar's Office within five (05) business days from the date on which the Registrar's Office posts the final grade for the term. • The Registrar's Office informs the Dean’s Office of the case. After investigation, if the Deans can mediate, no further action is required. Otherwise, the Registrar's Office organizes a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the grade. The grade determined after this evaluation shall be the final grade. In cases concerning the interpretation of a course policy, the Dean’s Office will defer to the course syllabus whenever possible and otherwise will make a final ruling on the

The student is required to attend an Academic Progress Meeting during which a Learning Contract will be created with specific conditions tailored to the individual situation. The Registrar's Office will be informed as a matter of record and follow-up. ### Question 98: I'm a third year student and don't know if I should do a capstone project then where should I go to get advice?  
### Answer: 

If you're a third-year student unsure about whether to undertake a capstone project, you should consult with the IS (Interdisciplinary Studies) faculty. They can provide guidance tailored to your specific situation and help you decide if a capstone project aligns with your academic and career goals. Additionally, they can assist you in refining your proposal and ensuring it meets all the necessary criteria. If you need a secondary advisor, they might also suggest finding one at another institution, especially if your primary advisor's expertise doesn't align well with your project idea. Remember, discussing your ideas early with the faculty is crucial to ensure your project is feasible and aligned with your educational objectives.

Allocation of advisor process As part of the application process, applicants will provide a first choice of primary and secondary advisor. It is not mandatory to have a secondary advisor. After the applications are

[Source: History Capstone Handbook - 2025-26.pdf, Page: 9]
The Capstone project is a year-long undertaking with less structure than a traditional course. It is certainly not the easiest way to complete your degree, and it may not be the most logical option for you, depending on your interests and your post-graduation plans. You should not consider it to be the default pathway to finishing your degree. One of the best reasons to undertake a Capstone project is if you enjoy doing historical research (which you will have sampled in Hands-On History and the research seminars you have completed) and want an opportunity to carry out a long-term research project. For such students, the Capstone year provides time and guidance that is unparalleled by any course or other opportunity at the undergraduate level. However, if you wish to graduate with distinction—an honorable goal— but you don’t particularly enjoy doing independent research, you may want to skip the Capstone and focus on GPA honors instead! Normally, the Capstone sequence begins in the Fall with Capstone I and

[Source: History Capstone Handbook - 2025-26.pdf, Page: 9]
requesting an external secondary advisor who does. Another way to approach this is to propose a Capstone project based on a 300-level research seminar that you have taken at Fulbright, or to ask the faculty for topic suggestions—that way, you are more likely to end up with a primary advisor who is also a subject-matter expert! The History Capstone Handbook, AY2025-26 student wishing to pursue journalism may want to complete their project in the form of a film or podcast. In general, although there can be exceptions, both thesis and non-thesis Capstones should ‘work up’ sources that do not figure extensively in existing scholarship, rather than taking the form of a literature review or commentary on existing secondary sources. This is something to discuss with a potential advisor. Guidelines for the Capstone by Thesis are included in Section 3 of this handbook. ### Question 99: I'm a member of Fulbright Basketball Club and going to attend a tournament. I need the official transcript and asking for some absence in classes then where should I get help?  
### Answer: 

You should contact the faculty or supervising staff responsible for the Fulbright Basketball Club. They will request a University Official Activity Excused Absence Request Form and submit it to the Dean’s Office, keeping Academic Affairs and Registrar’s Office informed. Remember, only faculty or supervising staff can request the excused absence for students. Afterward, you need to contact your instructors to make arrangements for any missed work and submit a summary of the tournament, proof of your attendance, and a reflection paper within the specified deadlines. Additionally, you should inform the Office of the Registrar upon your return. If you face any issues due to emergencies like hospitalization, contact the Academic Affairs team or Registrar’s Office during business hours. Lastly, ensure you are in good academic standing and not on probation to be excused from the class. Good luck with your tournament!

EXCEPTIONAL CIRCUMSTANCES: The University acknowledges that sometimes a student will experience circumstances that will impact their ability to fulfill the expectations of the University, including but not limited to assessment, attendance, and paying fees. Circumstances that may fall into this category are: • Exceptional medical circumstances, e.g., hospitalization or incapacitation through injury, illness, or mental health crisis. • Close bereavement, e.g., partner, child, parent, sibling, grandparent, and grandchild. Housemates or very close friends may also be considered as ‘close’, though evidence of the relationship may be required. • Victim of a serious crime • Disabilities for which reasonable adjustments are not yet in place and where the delay is not due to the student • Exceptional and unforeseeable transport difficulties e.g., major transport incidents, cancelled flights. This does not include everyday issues, e.g., traffic congestion, missed buses or trains. • Legal proceedings requiring

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 7]
STUDENT ENROLLMENT: 3.1 Course Load and Credit Hours Fulbright University Vietnam uses the “credit hour” as the quantum for course workload in the undergraduate program. A credit hour typically represents 3 hours of work during each week of a 16-week term. For a 4- credit hour course, a student would, therefore, be expected to put in 12 hours of work per week, including class time, for a total of 192 hours of work during a term. There are earned credits and attempted credits. Earned credits refer to the number of credit hours a student successfully completes with a grade of D or higher for letter grade options and a Pass for Pass/No Pass options. Attempted credits are the credit hours students enroll in and are recorded in the transcript, regardless of whether they complete the courses or pass them. This includes all courses for which a student receives a grade, including withdrawals (W), incompletes (I), repeats (RP), and failures (F). See section 4 for more details on different types of grades. To graduate

### Question 102: How to work with major report?  
### Answer: 

To work with major report, it's important to ensure that the Evaluation Report meets specific criteria. This involves defining clear objectives for the project, conducting a thorough literature review, developing a detailed project plan and timeline, and documenting the process comprehensively. The report should also include sections such as an introduction/motivation for the problem, a literature review, a problem statement/description, and proposed methods, plan, and timeline for Capstone 2. Additionally, the report should be submitted by the deadline on Canvas and should be appropriately formatted for academic submission. The Evaluation Report should critically evaluate the project against its goals using social studies theories and perspectives, and it should be clearly and logically structured with proper scaffolding and effective transitions. Finally, the report should be free of jargon and mechanical writing errors and assist the viewer in better understanding the project. Working with a non-academic advisor may also be beneficial for applied and creative projects, but this must be approved by the primary and secondary academic advisors from the SOCI major. It's crucial to meet all these requirements to produce a high-quality major report.

### Question 103: How many way can I fill in the requirements of EL?  
### Answer: 

You can fulfill the requirements of the Experiential Learning Program (ELP) in Fulbright's undergraduate program in three main ways:

1. By completing at least 4 credits and a maximum of 12 credits through the ELP streams, which are managed by Academic Affairs (AA), Career Services (CS), and Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation (CEI).
2. By taking electives that are approved by your advisor to count towards either elective or major requirements.
3. By applying for and completing an optional capstone pathway, which allows you to fulfill 8 credits of your major requirements via a capstone project. However, this option is only available to students who have completed 80 credits of coursework and have applied during the term prior to the first term of the capstone. 

So, there are three primary ways to meet the ELP requirements.

<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: CS_Capstone_Guideline_v2_Dec_20_2024.pdf, Page: 2]

Fulbright’s Experiential Learning Program (ELP) exists to create, standardize, and facilitate academic credit-bearing experiential learning experiences. All full-time, undergraduate, degree- seeking students must complete at least 04 credits and a maximum of 12 credits under the ELP as a graduation requirement. Current ELP streams are housed within Academic Affairs (AA), Career Services (CS), and Center for Entrepreneurship and Innovation (CEI), where each team is responsible for administrative and academic duties of their respective stream(s). The ELP operates within Fulbright’s undergraduate program’s standard operating procedures and is developed in consultation with undergraduate program leadership and faculty. For more details, please refer here https://onestop.fulbright.edu.vn/s/article/Experiential-Learning- Program 13.5  Electives To complete the degree, students are free to take elective courses from the Course Catalogue.
